<div class="container">
<div class="heading-text">
<h1 class="entry-title">Intelligent Thinking Through Habits of Mind</h1>
</div>
<div id="breadcrumbs">
<span property="itemListElement" typeof="ListItem"><a property="item" typeof="WebPage" title="Go to Mulberry Learning." href="https://mulberrylearning.com" class="home"><span property="name">Mulberry Learning</span></a><meta property="position" content="1"></span> &gt; <span property="itemListElement" typeof="ListItem"><a property="item" typeof="WebPage" title="Go to Programmes." href="https://mulberrylearning.com/programmes/" class="post post-page"><span property="name">Programmes</span></a><meta property="position" content="2"></span> &gt; <span property="itemListElement" typeof="ListItem"><span property="name" class="post post-page current-item">Intelligent Thinking Through Habits of Mind</span><meta property="url" content="https://mulberrylearning.com/programmes/habits-of-mind/"><meta property="position" content="3"></span></div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="pb-fw-wrap">

<div id="page-wrap">
<div class="inner-page-wrap has-no-sidebar clearfix">

<div class="clearfix " id="15564">
<div class="page-content clearfix">
<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<p class="impact-text" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #e90088;">How does your child behave when facing difficulties?</span></p>
<p class="impact-text" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #e90088;">Does he or she throw a tantrum and cry, simply give up, or look for ways to overcome the challenge?</span></p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="fw-row row-content-width asset-bg "><div class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb-row-container spb-row-content-width spb_parallax_asset sf-parallax parallax-content-height spb_content_element bg-type-cover col-sm-12  col-natural" data-v-center="true" data-top-style="" data-bottom-style="" style="background-color:#eeeeee;padding-left:0%;padding-right:0%;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px;">
<div class="spb_content_element" style="padding-top:0px;padding-bottom:0px;">
<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<p>As you observe your little ones work their way through everyday situations, you may start noticing distinctive patterns of behaviour. A childâ€™s formative years are exceptionally important as it is the period when they learn appropriate behaviours, boundaries and social skills that will remain with them for life. Especially when the world is becoming increasingly volatile, uncertain, complex, and ambiguous, these ways of coping with problems are budding indicators of how they would perform in future.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element spb_single_image noframe col-sm-12">
<div class="spb_wrapper"><figure class="lightbox animated-overlay overlay-alt clearfix"><picture decoding="async" class="attachment-full size-full">

</picture>

</div>
</div> </div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<p>Parents would already know that education is more than just learning about facts and knowledge, but the process of learning, such as the intricacies of posing questions, perseverance, thinking flexibly, and thirst for knowledge that are even more crucial for success. Learning these soft skills can take several lengthy processes of trial and error, and one may not even eventually succeed in cultivating these proficiencies.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
</div>
</div></div></div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<p class="impact-text" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #e90088;">But what if we tell you that there is a structured way of knowing how to behave intelligently and respond effectively to uncertainty or dilemmas that will better prepare your child for the future?</span></p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="fw-row row-content-width asset-bg "><div class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb-row-container spb-row-content-width spb_parallax_asset sf-parallax parallax-content-height spb_content_element bg-type-cover col-sm-12  col-natural" data-v-center="true" data-top-style="" data-bottom-style="" style="background-color:#eeeeee;padding-left:0%;padding-right:0%;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px;">
<div class="spb_content_element" style="padding-top:0px;padding-bottom:0px;">
<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h2 style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #800080;"><strong>What is Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup>?</strong></span></h2>
<p><strong>Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup></strong> is about knowing how to behave intelligently and respond effectively to uncertainty or dilemmas. Developed by <strong>Dr Arthur Costa, Emeritus Professor of Education at California State University</strong><strong>, </strong>Sacramento, and<strong> Co-Director of the Institute for Intelligent Behavior in El Dorado Hills, California</strong>, this framework provides children of all ages a set of intelligent thinking dispositions for autonomous learning, critical thinking and effective inquiry.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Just as how influential people like Steve Jobs and Mark Zuckerberg demonstrates positive traits like persistence and innovation, we too want our children to draw upon these positive ways of thinking that help them be more confident when confronted with difficulties. They will be able to ask good questions and become skilled at interacting with diverse groups of people. These habits also instill positive personality traits and behaviour in children to cultivate essential skills like strategic reasoning, insightfulness, perseverance and creativity, applying what they have learnt to an ever-expanding array of challenges not only in academic subjects but also in their lives, communities, and the world.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 column_container">
<div class="spb_wrapper">
<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">

<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<p class="impact-text" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #e90088;">While the Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup> framework has long been adopted by Singaporeâ€™s Ministry of Education to groom the <span style="color: #800080;">top 1% of students</span> under its Gifted Education Programme, Mulberry Learning is the<span style="color: #800080;"> first and only preschool network</span> globally certified by the <a href="https://www.habitsofmindinstitute.org/">Institute for Habits of Mind</a><sup>TM</sup>.</span></p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h2 style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #800080;">How Do We Incorporate Habits of Mind<strong><sup>TM </sup></strong>in Our Curriculum?<br>
</span></h2>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 column_container">
<div class="spb_wrapper">
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Formal Teaching</strong></h3>
<p>Every month, teachers at Mulberry Learning formally introduce a new habit during specially-designed lessons. Children will have opportunities to explore the meaning of the habit through engaging activities and emulate positive actions in accordance to the habit. Catchy slogans, which are suitable for preschoolers, are also used to help students remember!</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
</div>
</div>
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 column_container">
<div class="spb_wrapper">
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Reinforcements</strong></h3>
<p>Habits need to be reinforced repeatedly. Mulberry Learning teachers do so by consistently revisiting the habit throughout the term. When teachers chance upon teachable moments in lessons, playtime, mealtime, or during wash-up, they reiterate the specially-designed slogans.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 column_container">
<div class="spb_wrapper">
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Parental Involvement</strong></h3>
<p>We work closely with parents to provide them with updates on their childâ€™s progress in exemplifying Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup> in their day-to-day activities, alongside regular developmental updates. Special parenting workshops are also held from time to time to equip parents with knowledge, skills and activities that help them reinforce these habits at home.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
</div>
</div>
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 column_container">
<div class="spb_wrapper">
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Environment</strong></h3>
<p>Habits of Mind posters abound in every Mulberry Learning preschool as we meticulously craft the environment for successful planting of the Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup> seeds. While teachers themselves are role models for children, we also select monthly HoM Little Ambassadors in every preschool to recognise and celebrate the childâ€™s success in displaying positive dispositions both in school and at home.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<div class="spb_content_element" style="">
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h2 style="text-align: center;"><strong>Our Award-Winning Curriculum</strong></h2>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<p class="impact-text" style="text-align: center;">Find out how you can guide your little ones to cultivate good lifelong habits:</p>

<h3><strong>Creating, Imagining, Innovating</strong></h3>
<p>â€œI canâ€™t draw.â€ â€œI canâ€™t sing!â€ Some people think that creativity is innate and they can never gain that artistic flair. Yet, research has increasingly shown that children have the ability to produce original, novel, intelligent solutions and strategies if that capacity is nurtured. Through the plethora of STEAM enrichment programmes offered at Mulberry Learning, we provide opportunities to cultivate <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/dragons-martians-and-flying-chairs-remember-when-you-used-to-have-an-imagination/">creative, imaginative, and innovative</a> learners.</p>

<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Persisting</strong></h3>
<p>When posed with challenges, efficient problem solvers persevere even when a solution is not immediately apparent because they employ a wide variety of problem-solving strategies. Children often give up saying, â€œItâ€™s too hard!â€ or â€œI canâ€™t do this!â€ when faced with a problem. At Mulberry Learning, instead of providing all the answers, we <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/daddy-i-dont-know-how-why-giving-up-too-soon-is-bad-for-your-kids/">encourage students to persist</a> and work out problems on their own.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Listening with Understanding and Empathy</strong></h3>
<p>Many people assume that because they can comprehend words and their meaning, they can be a good listener. Yet sometimes, the loudest conversations are often the silent ones. Successful individuals spend an extravagant amount of time and energy to listen. They strive to relate to other peopleâ€™s point of view. Since studies have found that up to 80% of our communication with others are non-verbal, we need to be observant and identify non-verbal cues to listen well. <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/hello-are-you-even-listening-to-me/">Listening with understanding and empathy</a> requires us uncover the real message.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Questioning and Posing Problems</strong></h3>
<p>At Mulberry Learning, <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/mummy-why-is-that-aunty-so-fat/">children are encouraged to ask questions</a>, pose problems, and figure out the answers, with the help of their teachers! <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/project-inquiry">Inquiry-based learning</a> provides a rich opportunity for kids to widen and deepen their understanding and strengthen their appreciation of new knowledge. Students are able to act as little scientists, finding answers to their own questions through engaging in research, conducting mini-experiments, analysing their findings, and presenting their observations to their peers and parents.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Managing Impulsivity</strong></h3>
<p>Often, kids may shout out answers and act without thinking when interacting with their peers. They often react before considering the feelings of others. Yet, effective problem solvers take deliberate steps to <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/teach-children-to-stop-and-think/">think before they act</a>. They seek to clarify and understand instructions, develop a possible plan when approaching a problem, and suspend judgement about a problem until they fully understand it.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_video_widget spb_content_element col-sm-12">

<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Applying Past Knowledge to New Situations</strong></h3>
<p>Very often, our young ones approach tasks as if they were doing it for the first time. They are unable to find the links between past experiences and their current problems. Teachers and parents can help nudge kids in the correct direction by asking them questions like, â€œHave you seen this problem before?â€ or reminding them about similar experiences they faced in the past.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Gathering Data through All Senses</strong></h3>
<p>Children learn better and form stronger memory connections when <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/guess-what-mum-ive-just-discovered-the-world/">they engage with more senses in their learning process</a>. Through the various carefully-crafted <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/the-mulberry-edge/learning-spaces-2/">learning spaces</a> in our preschools, we encourage open, acute and alert sensory environments, allowing the little ones to absorb and retain much more information.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
</div>

<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 column_container">

<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Striving for Accuracy</strong></h3>
<p>As much as we provide a safe space for children to make mistakes, Mulberry Learning also encourages kids to <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/miss-the-mark-get-set-go-dont-let-your-child-get-used-to-making-small-mistakes/">strive for accuracy</a> and take pride in their work. This could be done by asking students follow-up questions when we notice an error in their work. Sometimes, a check-list could also help them to ensure accuracy in their tasks.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 column_container">

<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Thinking Flexibly</strong></h3>
<p>Children who think that their way is the only way to solve a problem would not be open to challenges and often avoid ambiguity. Yet, the world today is ambiguous and requires flexible thinking for success. Flexible thinkers have the ability to change their views about things when they acquire new information. They draw upon a range of problem-solving strategies to reach their goals and is important for success in future.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>
</div>
</div>
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-6 column_container">

<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Thinking About Your Thinking (Metacognition)</strong></h3>
<p>Adolescents are often oblivious of their own thinking while they are thinking. They seldom plan, reflect, or evaluate the quality of their thoughts. When asked how they solve a problem, they may reply, â€œI donâ€™t know!â€ and are not able to reiterate the sequences and steps they utilise during the entire process. At Mulberry Learning, our unique pedagogy designed by qualified and experienced educators make use of thinking words to encourage kids to start thinking about their own thinking.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Finding Humour</strong></h3>
<p>Laughter transcends all ages and it has positive effects on childrenâ€™s psychological functions. When lessons are fun, kids are more creative and are able to employ higher order thinking skills. Children who engage in finding humour are also able to perceive circumstances from a novel and often intriguing vantage point.</p>
</div>

<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h3><strong>Thinking Interdependently</strong></h3>
<p>â€œLeave me alone, I want to do it on my own!â€ Some children have underdeveloped social skills and do not work well in social situations. They prefer being on their own and are unable to cooperate with others. Even though having â€œme-timeâ€ is beneficial at times, kids need to learn how to work together and <a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/is-your-child-a-loner-this-may-be-a-problem-in-the-long-run/">think interdependently</a> with others to succeed in life.</p>

<div class="spb-row-container spb-row-content-width spb_parallax_asset sf-parallax parallax-content-height spb_content_element bg-type-cover col-sm-12  col-natural" data-v-center="true" data-top-style="" data-bottom-style="" style="background-color:#eeeeee;padding-left:0%;padding-right:0%;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px;">
<div class="spb_content_element" style="padding-top:0px;padding-bottom:0px;">
<section class="container"><div class="row"><div class="blank_spacer col-sm-12 " style="height:30px;"></div>
</div></section>
<section class="container"><div class="row">
<div class="spb_content_element col-sm-12 spb_text_column">
<div class="spb_wrapper clearfix">
<h2 style="text-align: center;"><strong>How can we assess if our children exemplify the Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup>?</strong></h2>
<h3 style="text-align: center;"><strong>Introducing THOMAS â€“ The Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup> Assessment Scale</strong></h3>
<p style="text-align: center;">Since employing Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup> requires a combination of multiple competencies, a comprehensive and structured method is required to observe and chart a childâ€™s development of these habits. The Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup> Assessment Tool (<a href="https://mulberrylearning.com/thomas/">THOMAS</a>), a psychometric tool to assess the thinking dispositions of young children was then developed by Dr. Henry Toi, our Research and Curriculum Dean, and an affiliate of The Institute for Habits of Mind<sup>TM</sup>.</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Teachers, with the help of parents, will complete the THOMAS questionnaire based on observations both at school and at home. The findings will provide a more accurate insight into the childâ€™s growth in these intelligent habits and help our research and development team improve the quality of curriculum.</p>
</div>
</div> </div></section>

<section id="text-6" class="widget widget_text clearfix"><div class="widget-heading clearfix"><h6>About Us</h6></div> <div class="textwidget"><p><img width="172" height="135" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20172%20135'%3E%3C/svg%3E" data-lazy-src="/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/footer-logo.png"><noscript><img width="172" height="135" src="/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/footer-logo.png"></noscript></p>
<p>Mulberry Learning prides itself on making the preschool experience both memorable and enjoyable while transforming a child into a competent explorer, an imaginative thinker, and a creative problem solver. Through our proprietary award-winning curriculum, unique Habits of Mind programme and dedicated staff who are passionate about imparting positive attitudes, Mulberry Learning holds strong in its promise to deliver a holistic education that nurtures the Future Ready Child.</p>
<p class="pink">A PREMIUM PRESCHOOL BRAND UNDER GLOBAL EDUHUB</p></div>
